тАШ рдХрд┐рдореБ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреИрд░реНрдШрддрдорд╕рдорд╛рд░реНрднрд╡рдореН ред рдЕрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рдпрд╛ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрдГ ред рдЕрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдЪ - рдХрд┐рдореБ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардГ рд╖рд│реВрдирд╛рд░реНрднрд╡рдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡реНрдпреВрд│реНрд╣реЗ рджрд╢рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗрд╜рд╣рдирд┐ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗ рдЖрд░реНрднрд╡рдВ рдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрдореН ред рддрддреНрд░ ‘рдХрд┐рдореБ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрддрджрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдЬрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрдореН ред тАШ рд╡реНрдпреВрд│реНрд╣рд╢реНрдЪреЗрддреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЦрдгреНрдбреЗ рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ - рдХрд┐рдореБ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЙрдк рдиреЛ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢рд╛рд░реНрднрд╡рдВ рдЪрддрд╕реНрд░рд╢реНрдЪ’ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рео. рео) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

161
R╠еbhus
D─лrghatamas Aucathya
14 verses: jagat─л 1тАУ13, triс╣гс╣нubh 14
This is a difficult hymn, but one essential for understanding the R╠еbhus and their relation to the Third Pressing. Its narrative tells how the R╠еbhus attained immortal ity and entered among the godsтАФor seems to. This theme is stated in verse 2 and elaborated in verses 11тАУ14. The R╠еbhus were priests who attained status as gods by their sacrificial performance. As gods they are worshiped in the Third Pressing, and therefore it is not surprising that the ritual acts by which they became gods are those

of the Third Pressing. For a detailed discussion of these acts, see the discussion by Brereton (2012).
The hymn begins by reference to one of the great acts of the R╠еbhus, their trans formation of a single soma cup into four soma cups. This act signifies their divin ization because the four cups represent four soma offerings to Indra and the three R╠еbhus. A single cup would have restricted the soma offering only to Indra. The hymn opens with the R╠еbhusтАЩ address to Agni, who has been sent by the gods. This dialogue takes place in the middle of the action, for apparently Agni has pointed to the camasa╠Б, the ritual soma cup, and the R╠еbhus are concerned that Agni thinks that they have insulted this soma cup in some way (vs. 1). But Agni reaffirms the command of the gods that the R╠еbhus create four cups out of this one, and he offers to make them gods (vs. 2). However, the R╠еbhus reply that they have much more to do as priests before they themselves become the objects of worship. First, they need to make a horse. Elsewhere they fashion the two horses of Indra, and it is to this act that verse 3 likely refers. The making of these horses points toward the H─Бriyojanagraha, an offering to Indra as he harnesses his horses to leave the ritual ground at the end of the Third Pressing (see also I.61тАУ63, 82). Second, they need to make a chariot, which can represent the hymn or the whole ritual. Third, they need to make a milk-cow, which represents the already-pressed soma stalks, which are made to yield additional soma in the Third Pressing. And finally they need to make young two who are old. The two might be the sacrificer and his wife or another pair. Once the R╠еbhus have accomplished all their great sac
rificial deeds, then they will be worthy to follow Agni to heaven (vs. 3). Tvaс╣гс╣нar is introduced in verse 4 probably in connection with another rite in the Third Pressing in which the Wife of the Sacrificer receives indirect access to the soma. Verse 5 returns to the four cups and we now learn that Tvaс╣гс╣нar, who had origi
nally made the one cup, is angry that the R╠еbhus are modifying his creation. The R╠еbhus protect themselves by taking on тАЬother names.тАЭ These тАЬother namesтАЭ may be their priestly offices, and by these names or priestly offices the тАЬmaidenтАЭ will rescue them. The hymn gives little clue to identity of the тАЬmaiden,тАЭ but she may be Sarasvat─л (cf. VI.49.7) or even Speech (V─Бc) herself. In either case, the words that the R╠еbhus master or the knowledge that they possess somehow protects them from the anger of Tvaс╣гс╣нar. Vs. 6 affirms that the R╠еbhus did succeed in becoming gods and divine recipients of soma.
In verse 7 the hymn returns to the sacrificial acts that made them immortal: the soma-pressing (see vs. 10), the rejuvenation of the aging pair, the creation of a horse, and the harnessing of the chariot that is the sacrifice or the hymn. Verse 8 marks a return to a dialogue, now between the R╠еbhus and the gods. According to S─Бyaс╣Зa, the тАЬwaterтАЭ and the тАЬrinse-water of mu├▒ja-reedsтАЭ that the gods offer the R╠еbhus are the soma of the first two pressings. This interpretation is contextually justifiable, but such a denigration of these first two pressings is unlikely. Oldenberg suggests that the gods first offer the R╠еbhus two inferior drinks and only then and finally the soma. If we take this approach, the first offering would be water, and the second might be a kind of faux-soma. The word m├║├▒ja approximates m┼л╠Бjavant, the mountain from which the real soma comes, and therefore the тАЬrinse-water of mu├▒ja-reedsтАЭ may represent an inferior approximation of soma. It is only the third time and in the third soma-pressing that the gods offer the R╠еbhus the real soma. Structurally verse 9 continues verse 8, since again three things are mentioned, of which the third is the best. However, it is difficult to say what the feminine noun described as vadharya╠Бnt─л тАЬweapon-wieldingтАЭ in p─Бda c might be, since the adjec
tive is otherwise unattested. According to S─Бyaс╣Зa, it is either the earth or a line of clouds and its weapon is lightning. Along similar lines, Geldner suggests that it is the rainy season and again that its weapon is lightning. Interpreting vadharya╠Бnt─л slightly differently, Witzel and Got┼Н understand it as the axe (sva╠Бdhiti) тАЬserving as a weapon.тАЭ We resolve the ellipsis by drawing its sense from the verb pra тИЪbr┼л
тАЬproclaimтАЭ in p─Бda c and the reference to spoken truths in p─Бda d. The first two R╠еbhus praise water and fire, which are essential to the sacrifice, but the third R╠еbhu recognizes true speech as the most essential element.
Verse 10 returns once again to the great sacrificial deeds of the R╠еbhus and this time especially to the soma that is prepared in the Third Pressing. In the Third Pressing soma stalks from the first two pressings are pressed again to yield addi tional soma. In verse 10 these stalks are the тАЬlame cowтАЭтАФlame because they have already been pressedтАФwhich are then soaked in water. The тАЬcarvingтАЭ of the cow is the re-pressing of the stalks, and the dung is the now thoroughly mangled stems of the soma plant. The place of 10d is not clear. Whoever the тАЬparentsтАЭ may be, the тАЬsonsтАЭ are likely the R╠еbhus or the priests that they represent.
The last sequence of verses, 11тАУ14, probably describes the ascent of the R╠еbhus to immortality, but even if this is correct, the details are obscure. At best we can point out a few possible identifications and a few possible interpretations. Agohya in verse 11 is probably the Sun as the тАЬUnconcealable One,тАЭ although he might also be Savitar. In I.110.2тАУ3 the R╠еbhusтАЩ attainment of immortality is connected with Agohya, and if Agohya is the Sun, then perhaps one stage in the R╠еbhusтАЩ ascent is to the sun. The Sun governs the year, and therefore the тАЬgrass on the heightsтАЭ may rep
resent the summer pasturage, and тАЬthe waters in the valleysтАЭ the winter pasturage. In verse 13 the identification of the goat and the dog as the sun and moon is doubt ful. It assumes that the basta╠Б тАЬgoatтАЭ is aja╠Б ekapa╠Бd, тАЬthe one-footed goat,тАЭ which elsewhere is the Sun. The identification of the moon as тАЬthe dogтАЭ follows ┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa XI.1.5.1, in which the moon is called the heavenly dog. In the last verse, the gods move throughout the visible world seeking the R╠еbhus, but perhaps they do not find them because they have gone from the visible world.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIs this our senior or our junior who has come (to us); has he come upon a message (from the gods); what is it we should say? Agni,brother, we revile not the ladle which is of exalted race; verily we assert the dignity of the wooden (implement).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The legend: the three с╣Ъbhus were engaged in a sacrifice and about to drink the Soma; the gods sent Agni to see what they were doing. Agni noticed that they resembled each other; Agni assumed a like form. The hymn refers to this form, calling himbrother, and questionign his comparative age. The next hymn states the purpose of Agni’s visit is to order the conversion of one spoon or ladle, camasa, used for drinking Soma, or for libations, into four spoons

Griffith

WHY hath the Best, why hath the Youngest come to us? Upon what embassy comes he? What have we said?
We have not blamed the chalice of illustrious birth. We, Brother Agni, praised the goodness of the wood.

English translation:

тАЬMake fourfold the single ladle; so the gods command you; and for that purpose have I come, sons of Sudhanvan; if you accomplish this, you will be entitled to sacrifices along with the gods.тАЭ

[Agni:] тАЬ тАШMake the one cup to be fourтАЩтАФthat the gods said to you. For that I have come to you.

Griffith

The chalice that is single make ye into four: thus have the Gods commanded; therefore am I come.
If, O Sudhanvan’s Children, ye will do this thing ye shall participate in sacrifice with Gods.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThen said they, in answer to Agni, the messenger (of the gods). Whatever is to be done, whether a horse is to be made, or a car is to be made, or a cow is to be made, or the two (old parents) are to be made young, having done all these (acts), Brother Agni, we are then ready to do (what you desire) to be done.тАЭ

What to the envoy Agni in reply ye spake, A courser must be made, a chariot fashioned here,
A cow must be created, and the Twain made young. When we have done these things, Brother, we turn to you.

рд╣реЗ рдЛрднрд╡рдГ рддрддреН рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдВ рдпрдерд╛ ‘рдЪрдХреГрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рдХреГрддрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рдпреВрдпрдореН рдЕрдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрдд рдкреНрд░рд╢реНрдирдВ рдХреБрд░реБрдд рее рдХрд░реЛрддреЗрд░реНрд▓рд┐рдЯрдГ рдХреНрд╡рд╕реБрдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдпрджреНрдпрдкрд┐ рдЛрднреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдПрдХрд╕реНрдп рдирд╛рдо рддрдерд╛рдкрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдердореНрдпрд╛рддреН тАШрдЫрддреНрд░рд┐рдгреЛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐рд╡рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╜рдкрд┐ рдЛрднрд╡рдГ’ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдХрд┐рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрдпрдГ рд╕рдГ рджреВрддрдГ рдХреНрд╡реЗрджрднреВрддреН рдХреБрддреНрд░ рдЧрддрдГ ред рд╕ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рдХ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред рдпрдГ рдпреЛ рджреВрддрдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЖрдЬрдЧрдиреН рдЖрдЧрдорддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВрднреВрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рдпрджрд╛ рдЕрдпрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдЪрддреБрд░рдГ рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреН рдЪрдорд╕рд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╡рд╛рдЦреНрдпрддреН рдЕрднрд┐рдкрд╢реНрдпрддрд┐ рее рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддреЗрд░реНрд▓реБрдЩрд┐ тАв рдЕрд╕реНрдпрддрд┐рд╡рдХреНрддрд┐рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд┐┬░ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреНрд▓реЗрдГ рдЕрдЩрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ рее рдЖрджрд┐рддреН рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореЗрд╡ рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рддрд╕реНрдп рдЪрдорд╕рд╕реНрдпреЛрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХрдГ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХреЛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рдЧреНрдирд╛рд╕реБ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрд╖реБ ред рдореЗрдирд╛ рдЧреНрдирд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдгрд╛рдореН’ ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. рей. реирез) рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдирдЬреЗ рдиреНрдпрдХреНрддреЛрд╜рднреВрддреН ред рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдореН рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рдирдореН рдЕрдордиреНрдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рдЕрдЮреНрдЬреЗрд░реНрд▓рд┐рдЯрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреНрдиреБрдбреНрджреНрд╡рд┐рд╣рд▓рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдиреБрдЯреН ред рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛрд╜рдиреБрдирд╛рд╕рд┐рдХрд▓реЛрдкрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

Having done these things, R╠еbhus, you asked this: тАЬJust where has he gone who came here to us as a messenger?тАЭ
When he caught sight of the four cups that were made, just then Tvaс╣гс╣нar was anointed among the Wives (of the Gods).

Griffith

When thus, O Rbhus, ye had done ye questioned thus, Whither went he who came to us a messenger?
Then Tvastar, when he viewed the four wrought chalices, concealed himself among the Consorts of the Gods.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЪрдХреГрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕ рдЛрднрд╡реЛ рдпреЛ рджреВрддреЛ рди рдЖрдЬрдЧрдиреН рд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ рдХреНрд╡рд╛рднреВрджрд┐рддрд┐ рддрджрд┐рддреНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреЛрд╜рдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрддред рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдпрджрд╛ рдЪрдорд╕рд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдЦреНрдпрддреНрддрджрд╛ рд╕ рдЪрддреБрд░рдГ рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рджрд╛рддреНрд╕ рдЗрддреН рдЧреНрдирд╛рд╕реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд░реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдирдЬреЗ рее рек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЪрдХреГрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ) рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд░рдГ (рдЛрднрд╡рдГ) рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдГред рдЛрднреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж рейред резрелред (рддрддреН) (рдЕрдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрдд) рдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреБ (рдХреНрд╡) рдХрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рдЕрднреВрддреН) рднрд╡рддрд┐ (рдпрдГ) (рд╕реНрдпрдГ) (рджреВрддрдГ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЖ) (рдЕрдЬрдЧрдиреН) рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ (рдпрджрд╛) (рдЕрд╡рд╛рдЦреНрдпрддреН) рдкреНрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдкрдпреЗрддреН (рдЪрдорд╕рд╛рдиреН) рдореЗрдШрд╛рдиреН (рдЪрддреБрд░рдГ) рд╡рд╛рдпреНрд╡рдЧреНрдирд┐рдЬрд▓рднреВрдореАрдГ (рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреН) (рдЖрддреН) (рдЗрддреН) (рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛) рддрдиреВрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ (рдЧреНрдирд╛рд╕реБ) рдЧрдиреНрддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБ рднреВрдорд┐рд╖реБ (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рдирд┐) (рдЖрдирдЬреЗ) рдЕрд╕реНрдпреЗрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд▓рдпреЗрддреН рее рек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б said: let us slay those who have profaned the ladle, (designed) for the drinking of the gods; then they made use of other names for one another as the libation was poured out; and the maiden (mother) propitiated them by different appellations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Then they made us of other names: a legend accounts for the origin of the names of the chief officiating priests; to evade the indignation of Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, the с╣Ъbhus assumed the titles: adhvaryu, hot─Б and udgat─Б;an individual engaged in priestly functions at a sacrifice is to be always addressed by these titles, and never by his own name; propitiated themby different appellations: anyair en─Бn kany─Б n─Бmabhiс╕е sparat: kany─Б = svotp─Бdayitr─л m─Бt─Б, a mother self-engendering

Jamison Brereton

When Tvaс╣гс╣нar said, тАЬWe shall smash those who have insulted the cup that gives drink to the godsтАЭтАФ
they [=the R╠еbhus] make other names for themselves during the soma-pressingтАФby their other names the maiden will rescue them.

Griffith

As Tvastar thus had spoken, Let us slay these men who have reviled the chalice, drinking-cup of Gods,
They gave themselves new names when Soma juice was shed, and under these new names the Maiden welcomed them.

Geldner

Als Tvastri sprach: “Wir wollen sie erschlagen, die die Becher f├╝r den G├╢ttertrank getadelt haben”, da nahmen sie bei dem Somaopfer andere Namen an. Unter anderen Namen brachten sie die Jungfrau in Sicherheit.

Grassmann

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSons of Sudhanvan, from a hideless (cow) you have formed a living one; by your marvellous acts you have made your aged parents young; from one horse you have fabricated another; harness now your chariot, and repair unto the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

From the hide you made the cow to flow (milk) by your insights. You made those young who were the aging pair.
O sons of Sudhanvan, you fashioned a horse from a horse, and having hitched up the chariot, you journeyed toward the gods.

Griffith

Ye by your wisdom brought a cow from out a hide; unto that ancient Pair ye gave again their youth.
Out of a horse, Sudhanvan’s Sons, ye formed a horse: a chariot ye equipped, and went unto the Gods.

Geldner

Aus dem Fell lie├Яet ihr durch eure Erfindungsgabe die Kuh herauslaufen; die beiden Alten machtet ihr jung. Ihr S├╢hne des Sudhanvan, aus einem Pferd zimmertet ihr ein zweites Pferd. Ihr schirrtet den Wagen an und fuhret zu den G├╢ttern.

Grassmann

Mit Weisheit l├╢stet ihr die Kuh aus ihrem Fell, die beiden Alten habt ihr wieder jung gemacht; Aus einem Ross, Sudhanvans S├╢hne, noch ein Ross; geschirrten Wagens fuhret zu den G├╢ttern ihr.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey, (the gods), have said, sons of Sudhanvan, drink of this water, (the Soma); or drink that which has been filtered through the mu├▒ja grass; or, if you be plural ased with neither of these, be exhilarated (by that which is drunk) at the third (daily) sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъbhus may be participants of the libations offered at dawn or at noon; the right of the с╣Ъbhus to share in the third, or evening sacrifice is always acknowledged

Jamison Brereton

[The R╠еbhus to the gods:] тАЬYou said, тАШDrink this water, or drink this, the rinse-water of mu├▒ja-reeds.
Sons of Sudhanvan, if you do not in any way find satisfaction in this, you shall find exhilaration in the Third Pressing rite.тАЩтАЭ

Griffith

Drink ye this water, were the words ye spake to them; or drink ye this, the rinsing of the Mu├▒ja-grass.
If ye approve not even this, Sudhanvan’s Sons, then at the third libation gladden ye yourselves.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWaters are the most excellent said one (of them). Agni is that most excellent, said another; the third declared to many the Earth (to be the most excellent), and thus speaking true things the с╣Ъbhus divided the ladle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The earth: vardhayant─лm = a line of clouds or the earth: vadhaс╕е arkaс╕е (Nirukta 2.20.7)

Jamison Brereton

One (R╠еbhu) said, тАЬWaters are most important,тАЭ and the other said, тАЬFire is most important.тАЭ
(The third) one proclaimed the weapon-wielding (speech?) from among the many. Speaking truths, you carved the cups.

Griffith

Most excellent are waters, thus said one of you; most excellent is Agni, thus another said.
Another praised to many a one the lightning cloud. Then did ye shape the cups, speaking the words of truth.

Geldner

Das Wasser ist das Wichtigste”, so sprach der eine. “Das Feuer ist das Wichtigste”, so sprach der andere. Der eine gab der Gewitterzeit vor vielen den Vorzug. Wahre Reden f├╝hrend schnitztet ihr die Becher.

Grassmann

Der eine sprach: ┬╗das Wasser ist das herrlichste┬л; der andre sprach: ┬╗Nein, Feuer ist das herrlichste┬л; Der dritte pries um vieles mehr das Blitzgeschoss; so Gutes redend bildetet die Becher ihr.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOne pours the red water (the blood) upon the ground; one cuts the flesh, divided into fragments by the chopper; and a third seperates the excrement from the other parts; in what manner may the parents (of the sacrifice) render assistance to their sons?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The с╣Ъbhus are identified with the priests employed in the sacrifice of a victim; the parents of the sacrifice: the parents pitс╣Ыs, = the instrumental tutor of the ceremony and his wife

Jamison Brereton

One drives the lame cow down to the water. One carves the flesh, carried here with a basket.
Up till sunset one bore away the dung. Have the parents given help to their sons?

Griffith

One downward to the water drives the crippled cow, another trims the flesh brought on the carving-board.
One carries off the refuse at the set of sun. How did the Parents aid their children in their task!

Geldner

Einer treibt die lahme Kuh zum Wasser hinab; einer zerlegt das Fleisch, das im Korb gebracht wird. Bis Sonnenuntergang trug einer den Dung fort. Haben wohl die beiden Eltern ihren S├╢hnen dabei geholfen?

Grassmann

Der eine treibt die lahme Kuh zum Wasser hin, der andre schneidet auf dem Brett das Fleisch zurecht, Der dritte kehrt am Abend allen Mist hinweg; ob wol den Aeltern wohlgefiel der S├╢hne Thun?

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рдкрд┐рддрд╛-рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЧреМрдПрдВ рдмрдЫрдбрд╝реЗ рдХреЛ рд╕реБрдЦ рдЪрд╛рд╣рддреА, рджреБрдГрдЦ рд╕реЗ рдмрдЪрд╛рддреА рд╡рд╛ рдмрд╣реЗрд▓рд┐рдпрд╛ рдорд╛рдВрд╕ рдХреЛ рд▓реЗрдХреЗ рдЕрдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯ рдХреЛ рдЫреЛрдбрд╝реЗ рд╡рд╛ рд╡реИрджреНрдп рд░реЛрдЧреА рдХреЗ рдорд▓ рдХреЛ рджреВрд░ рдХрд░реЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рджреБрд░реНрдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреГрдердХреН рдХрд░ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рди рдХреЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпрдереИрдХрдГ рд╢реНрд░реЛрдгрд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдореБрджрдХрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╡рд╛рдЬрддрд┐ рдпрдереИрдХрдГ рд╕реВрдирдпрд╛рднреГрддрдВ рдорд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рдкрд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐ рдпрдереИрдХреЛ рдирд┐рдореНрд░реБрдЪрдГ рд╢рдХреГрджрдкрд╛рднрд░рддреНрддрдерд╛ рдкрд┐рддрд░реМ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рджреБрдкрд╛рд╡рддреБрдГ рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬс╣Ъbhus, leaders (of the rains), you have caused the grass to grow upon the high plural ces; you have caused the waters to flow over the low plural ces; for (the promotion of) good works; as you have reposed for a while in the dwelling of the unapprehensible (Sun), so desist not today from (the discharge of) this (your function).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъbhus are identified in this and following hymns with the rays of the sun, as the instrumental uments of the rain and the causes of fertility; ─Бdityara┼Ыmayo api с╣Ыbhava ucyante: (Nirukta 11.16); unapprehensible Sun: agohyasya gс╣Ыhe: agohya = a name of the sun (Nirukta); who is not to be hidden, aguhan─лya;or, agrahaс╣З─лya, not to be apprehended, literally or metaphorically; so desist not: idam n─Бnugacchatha; anusс╣Ыtya na gacchatha, having come forth, go not away without doing this,idam, your office of sending down rain for as long a period as you repose in the solar orb; a truism is explained in Nirukta: y─Бvat tatra bhavatha na t─Бvadiha bhavatha, as long as you are there, you are not here

Jamison Brereton

You made grass for him on the heights and waters in the valleys by your skillful work, o men,
when you slept in the house of Agohya: you do not continue that here today, o R╠еbhus.

Griffith

On the high places ye have made the grass for man, and water in the valleys, by your skill, O Men.
Rbhus, ye iterate not to-day that act of yours, your sleeping in the house of him whom naught can hide.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs you glide along enveloping the regions (in clouds); where, then, are the parents (of the world)? curse him who arrests your arm; reply sternly to him who speaks disrespectfully (to you).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The parents of the world: the sun and the moon, the protectors of the world, which, during the rains, are hidden by the clouds; who speaks disrespectfully: yaс╕е pr─Бbrav─лt pra tasm─Б abrav─лtana: pra prefixed to br┼л = either to speak harshly or kindly, to censure or to praise

Jamison Brereton

When, having shut your eyes, you crept around the living worlds, where were your loving parents? You cursed him who took your arm. Who made a declaration (to you), to him you also made a declaration.

Griffith

As, compassing them round, ye glided through the worlds, where had the venerable Parents their abode?
Ye laid a curse on him who raised his arm at you: to him who spake aloud to you ye spake again.

Geldner

Als ihr mit geschlossenen Augen die Wesen umschlichet, wo waren da eure z├дrtlichen Eltern? Ihr fluchtet dem, der euch am Arme fa├Яte. Wer euch anredete, dem standet ihr Rede.

Grassmann

Als ihr geschlossnen Auges durch die Wesen schlicht, wo weilte damals eur geliebtes Aelternpaar? Ihr fluchtet dem, der hemmend in den Arm euch fiel; dem, der euch gr├╝sste, botet ihr den Gegengruss.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬс╣Ъbhus, reposing in the solar orb, you inquire: who awakens us, unapprehensive (Sun), to this office (of sending rain). The Sun replies: the awakener is the wind; and the year (being ended), you again today light up this (world).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The awakener is the wind: ┼Ыv─Бnam bodhayit─Бram = the awakener is the dog; but, ┼Ыv─Бnam = antarkс╣гe svasantam v─Бyum, the reposer in the firmament, the wind; saс╣Гvatsare idam ady─Б vyakhyata, you have made this world today luminous, after the year has expired; i.e. the rainy season has passed, the rays of the sun and moon are again visible

Jamison Brereton

After you slept, R╠еbhus, you asked this: тАЬWho awakened us here, o Agohya?тАЭ
The billy-goat [=the Sun?] said the dog [=the Moon?] was the awakener. Here today, after a year, you opened your eyes.

Griffith

When ye had slept your fill, ye Rbhus, thus ye asked, O thou whom naught may hide, who now hath wakened us?
The goat declared the hound to be your wakener. That day, in a full year, ye first unclosed our eyes.

Geldner

Als ihr Ribhu┬┤s ausgeschlafen hattet, da fragtet ihr: " Agohya! Wer hat uns da geweckt?" Der Bock nannte den Hund als Wecker. Nach Jahresfrist habt ihr euch heute in dieser Welt umgeschaut.

Grassmann

Als, Ribhu’s, ihr dann ausgeschlafen fragtet ihr: Agohja, sprich, wer hat uns eben aufgeweckt? Da gab der Bock den Hund als euren Wecker an; nach einem Jahre schlugt ihr da die Augen auf.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSons of Strength, the Maruts, desirous of your coming, advance from the sky; Agni comes (to meet you) from the earth; the wind traverses the firmament; and Varuс╣Зa comes with undulating waters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Maruts travel through heaven, Agni along the earth; the Wind here travels through the midspace;
Varuс╣Зa travels through the waters and seasтАФseeking you, o sons of strength.
The following two hymns treat the Horse Sacrifice (A┼Ыvamedha) and are the only absolutely clear reflections of this ritual in the R╠еgveda.

Griffith

The Maruts move in heaven, on earth this Agni; through the mid-firmament the Wind approaches.
Varuna comes in the sea’s gathered waters, O Sons of Strength, desirous of your presence.

Geldner

Am Himmel gehen die Marut, auf der Erde Agni, der Wind geht im Luftraum; in den Wassern, in den Meeren geht Varuna, indem sie euch suchen, ihr Kinder der Kraft.

Grassmann

Am Himmel gehn die Maruts, auf der Erde geht Agni, und der Wind hier durch die L├╝fte; und Varuna geht durch des Meeres Fluten; sie alle suchen euch, der St├дrke S├╢hne.

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп, рдкрд╡рди, рднреВрдорд┐, рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐, рд╡рд╛рдпреБ, рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд░реБрдг рдФрд░ рдЬрд▓реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдПрдХ рд╕рд╛рде рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕ рд╣реИ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╡рд╛рд╕ рдХрд░ рдирд┐рддреНрдп рд╕реБрдЦрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдмрд▓реА рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рее резрек реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐ рдХреЗ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдЗрдХрд╕рдард╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЫрдард╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╢рд╡рд╕реЛ рдирдкрд╛рддреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпрдерд╛ рдорд░реБрддреЛ рджрд┐рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╣ рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ред рдЕрдпрдордЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрднреВрдореНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд╛рддреЛрд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗрдг рдЪ рд╕рд╣ рдпрд╛рддрд┐ рд╡рд░реБрдгреЛрд╜рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реИрдГ рд╕рд╣ рдпрд╛рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдирд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреЛ рдЬрдирд╛ рдпрд╛рдиреНрддреБ рее резрек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджрд┐рд╡рд╛) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЗрдг рд╕рд╣ (рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдорд╛ рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡рдГ (рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддреН (рдЕрдпрдореН) (рд╡рд╛рддрдГ) рдордзреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗрдг) (рдпрд╛рддрд┐) (рдЕрджреНрднрд┐рдГ) рдЬрд▓реИрдГ (рдпрд╛рддрд┐) (рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ) рдЙрджрд╛рдирдГ (рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реИрдГ) рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░реИрдГ (рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН) (рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ) (рд╢рд╡рд╕рдГ) рдмрд▓рд╡рддрдГ (рдирдкрд╛рддрдГ) рди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ рдкрд╛рддреН рдкрддрдирдВ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ рее резрек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдорд░реБрддреЛрд░реНрднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреНрдпреЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдпреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдпреЛрд░реНрд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛рд╜рдкрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд╛рд╕реЛрд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реБрдЦрдмрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рее резрек реердЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рдПрдХрд╖рд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп, рдорд░реБрдд, рднреВрдореА, рдЕрдЧреНрдиреА, рд╡рд╛рдпреВ, рдЕрдВрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рд╡ рд╡рд░реБрдг рдЖрдгрд┐ рдЬрд▓ рдПрдХрддреНрд░ рд░рд╛рд╣рддрд╛рдд рддрд╕реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рд░рд╛рд╣реВрди рдирд┐рддреНрдп рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╡ рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рди рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резрек рее
